Case Study Description
Contoso Ltd
Overview
Contoso, Ltd. is a manufacturing company that has offices
worldwide. Contoso works with partner organizations to bring products to
market.
Contoso products are manufactured by using blueprint files that
the company authors and maintains.
Existing Environment
Currently, Contoso uses multiple types of servers for business
operations, including the following:
✑ File servers
✑ Domain controllers
✑ Microsoft SQL Server
servers
Your network contains an Active Directory forest named
contoso.com. All servers and client computers are joined to Active Directory.
You have a public-facing application named App1.
App1 is comprised of the following three tiers:
✑ A SQL database
✑ A web front end
✑ A processing middle tier

Each tier is comprised of five virtual machines. Users access
the web front end by using HTTPS only.
Requirements
Planned Changes
Contoso plans to implement
the following changes to the infrastructure:
- Move all the tiers of App1 to Azure.
- Move the existing product blueprint files to Azure Blob
storage.
- Create a hybrid directory to support an upcoming Microsoft
Office 365 migration project.
Technical Requirements
Contoso must meet the
following technical requirements:
✑ Move all the virtual
machines for App1 to Azure.
✑ Minimize the number of
open ports between the App1 tiers.
✑ Ensure that all the
virtual machines for App1 are protected by backups.
✑ Copy the blueprint files
to Azure over the Internet.
✑ Ensure that the blueprint
files are stored in the archive storage tier.
✑ Ensure that partner
access to the blueprint files is secured and temporary.

✑ Prevent user passwords or
hashes of passwords from being stored in Azure.
✑ Use unmanaged standard
storage for the hard disks of the virtual machines.
✑ Ensure that when users
join devices to Azure Active Directory (Azure AD), the users use a mobile phone
to verify their identity.
Minimize administrative effort whenever possible.
User Requirements
Contoso identifies the
following requirements for users:
✑ Ensure that only users
who are part of a group named Pilot can join devices to Azure AD.
✑ Designate a new user
named Admin1 as the service administrator of the Azure subscription.
✑ Admin1 must receive email
alerts regarding service outages.
✑ Ensure that a new user
named User3 can create network objects for the Azure subscription.
Question: 602 CertyIQ
You are planning the move of App1 to Azure.
You create a network security group (NSG).
You need to recommend a solution to provide users with access to App1.
What should you recommend?
A. Create an incoming security rule for port 443 from the Internet. Associate the NSG to the subnet that
contains the web servers.
B. Create an outgoing security rule for port 443 from the Internet. Associate the NSG to the subnet that
contains the web servers.
C. Create an incoming security rule for port 443 from the Internet. Associate the NSG to all the subnets.
D. Create an outgoing security rule for port 443 from the Internet. Associate the NSG to all the subnets.

Answer: A
Explanation:
Incoming and the web server subnet only, as users access the web front end by using HTTPS only.
Note Scenario: You have a public-facing application named App1. App1 is comprised of the following three
tiers:
✑ A SQL database
✑ A web front end
✑ A processing middle tier
Each tier is comprised of five virtual machines. Users access the web front end by using HTTPS only.

joined to Active Directory.

✑ A web front end
✑ A processing middle tier

Question: 603 CertyIQ
HOTSPOT -
You implement the planned changes for NSG1 and NSG2.
For each of the following statements, select Yes if the statement is true. Otherwise, select No.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.
Hot Area:

Answer:
Explanation:
Box 1: Yes-
The rule is configured inbound from VM1 and VM2 will allow the traffic because of stateful firewall inspection,
the traffic is allowed to come in. If the traffic is initiated from VM2 them it wouldn't work.-
Box 2: Yes -
ICMP is not blocked -ping will be allow because the vnets are already peered
traffic is initiated from VM2 and the outbound rule will block it.
Box 3: No -
NSG2 blocks RDP from VM2 -
Reference:
https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/virtual-network/network-security-group-how-it-works
Case Study Description:
Litware, inc.
Overview
Litware, Ltd. is a consulting company that has a main office in Montreal and two branch offices in Seattle
and New York.

The Montreal office has 2,000 employees. The Seattle office has 1,000 employees. The New York office has
200 employees.

as DNS servers and host the Litware.com DNS zone.
Litware has finance, human resources, sales, research, and information technology departments. Each
department has an organizational unit (OU) that contains all the accounts of that respective department.
All the user accounts have the department attribute set to their respective department. New users are
added frequently.
Litware.com contains a user named User1.
All the offices connect by using private links.
Litware has data centers in the Montreal and Seattle offices. Each data center has a firewall that can be
configured as a VPN device.

The virtualization environment contains the servers in the following table.

1GB of memory.

The network security team implements several network security groups (NSGs).

Litware plans to implement the following changes:
• Deploy Azure ExpressRoute to the Montreal office.
• Migrate the virtual machines hosted on Server1 and Server2 to Azure.
• Synchronize on-premises Active Directory to Azure Active Directory (Azure AD).
• Migrate App1 and App2 to two Azure web apps named webApp1 and WebApp2.

Technical requirements
Litware must meet the following technical requirements:
• Ensure that WebApp1 can adjust the number of instances automatically based on the load and can scale
up to five instance*.

the Montreal office.
• Ensure that routing information is exchanged automatically between Azure and the routers in the
Montreal office.

• Connect the New Your office to VNet1 over the Internet by using an encrypted connection.

• Minimize costs whenever possible.
Question: 604 CertyIQ
You need to ensure that you can add VM1 and VM2 to the backend pool of LB1.
What should you do first?
A. Redeploy VM1 and VM2 to the same availability zone.
B. Connect VM2 to VNET1/Subnet1.
C. Create a new NSG and associate the NSG to VNET1/Subnet1.
D. Redeploy VM1 and VM2 to the same availability set.
Answer: D
Explanation:
Redeploy VM1 and VM2 to the same availability set.
For a LB basic it is required that the virtual machines are in a single availability set or scale set of virtual
machines
"An existing VM cannot be added to an availability set after it is created."
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/virtual-machines/linux/tutorial-availability-sets
A VM can only be added to an availability set when it is created.
"https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/virtual-machines/windows/change-availability-set"
If they are already in the same availability set , then you don't need to do B anyway, your a good little Azure
admin, keep it up and create your backend pool with them in it. The fact that this question is being asked with
no option of 'nothing' means they are not already in the same AS.

✑ Create an Azure AD security group named Group4.
✑ Back up the Azure file shares and virtual machines by using Azure Backup.
✑ Trigger an alert if VM1 or VM2 has less than 20 GB of free space on volume C.
✑ Enable User1 to create Azure policy definitions and User2 to assign Azure policies to RG1.
✑ Create an internal Basic Azure Load Balancer named LB1 and connect the load balancer to VNET1/Subnet1
✑ Enable flow logging for IP traffic from VM5 and retain the flow logs for a period of eight months.
✑ Whenever possible, grant Group4 Azure role-based access control (Azure RBAC) read-only permissions to
the Azure file shares.
Question: 605 CertyIQ
You need to add VM1 and VM2 to the backend pool of LB1.
What should you do first?
A. Connect VM2 to VNET1/Subnet1.
B. Redeploy VM1 and VM2 to the same availability zone.
C. Redeploy VM1 and VM2 to the same availability set.
D. Create a new NSG and associate the NSG to VNET1/Subnet1.
Answer: C
Explanation:
No point in Connecting VM2 to VNET1/Subnet1 as you are going to have to redeploy it anyway.

"An existing VM cannot be added to an availability set after it is created."
https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/virtual-machines/linux/tutorial-availability-sets
A VM can only be added to an availability set when it is created.
"https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/virtual-machines/windows/change-availability-set"
If they are already in the same availability set , then you don't need to do B anyway, your a good little Azure
admin, keep it up and create your backend pool with them in it. The fact that this question is being asked with
no option of 'nothing' means they are not already in the same AS.

Case Study Description:
Contoso Ltd (Consulting Company)
Case study
This is a case study. Case studies are not timed separately. You can use as much exam time as you would like

Case Study Description
Case study
This is a case study. Case studies are not timed separately. You can use as much exam time as you
would like to complete each case. However, there may be additional case studies and sections on this
exam. You must manage your time to ensure that you are able to complete all questions included on this exam

case study. Case studies might contain exhibits and other resources that provide more information about the

to make changes before you move to the next section of the exam. After you begin a new section, you cannot

To start the case study
To display the first question in this case study, click the Next button. Use the buttons in the left pane to

Overview
Contoso, Ltd. is a manufacturing company that has offices worldwide. Contoso works with partner
organizations to bring products to market.
Contoso products are manufactured by using blueprint files that the company authors and maintains.
Existing Environment
Currently, Contoso uses multiple types of servers for business operations, including the following:
· File servers
· Domain controllers
· Microsoft SQL Server servers
Your network contains an Active Directory forest named contoso.com. All servers and client computers are
joined to Active Directory.
You have a public-facing application named App1. App1 is comprised of the following three tiers:
· A SQL database
· A web front end
· A processing middle tier
Each tier is comprised of five virtual machines. Users access the web front end by using HTTPS only.
Requirements
Planned Changes
Contoso plans to implement the following changes to the infrastructure:
· Move all the tiers of App1 to Azure.
· Move the existing product blueprint files to Azure Blob storage.
· Create a hybrid directory to support an upcoming Microsoft Office 365 migration project.

Technical Requirements
Contoso must meet the following technical requirements:
· Move all the virtual machines for App1 to Azure.
· Minimize the number of open ports between the App1 tiers.
· Ensure that all the virtual machines for App1 are protected by backups.
· Copy the blueprint files to Azure over the Internet.
· Ensure that the blueprint files are stored in the archive storage tier.
· Ensure that partner access to the blueprint files is secured and temporary.
· Prevent user passwords or hashes of passwords from being stored in Azure.
· Use unmanaged standard storage for the hard disks of the virtual machines.
· Ensure that when users join devices to Azure Active Directory (Azure AD), the users use a mobile phone to
· verify their identity.
· Minimize administrative effort whenever possible.
User Requirements
Contoso identifies the following requirements for users:
· Ensure that only users who are part of a group named Pilot can join devices to Azure AD.
· Designate a new user named Admin1 as the service admin for the Azure subscription.
· Admin1 must receive email alerts regarding service outages.
· Ensure that a new user named User3 can create network objects for the Azure subscription.

Case Study Description:
Overview
Litware, Inc. is a consulting company that has a main office in Montreal and two branch offices in Seattle and
New York.
The Montreal office has 2,000 employees. The Seattle office has 1,000 employees. The New York office has
200 employees.
All the resources used by Litware are hosted on-premises.
Litware creates a new Azure subscription. The Azure Active Directory (Azure AD) tenant uses a domain named
litware.onmicrosoft.com. The tenant uses the Premium P1 pricing tier.
Existing Environment
The network contains an Active Directory forest named litware.com. All domain controllers are configured as
DNS servers and host the litware.com DNS zone.
Litware has finance, human resources, sales, research, and information technology departments. Each
department has an organizational unit (OU) that contains all the accounts of that respective department. All
the

user accounts have the department attribute set to their respective department. New users are added
frequently.
Litware.com contains a user named User1.
All the offices connect by using private connections.
Litware has data centers in the Montreal and Seattle offices. Each office has a firewall that can be configured
as a VPN device.
All infrastructure servers are virtualized. The virtualization environment contains the servers in the following
table.
Litware uses two web applications named App1 and App2. Each instance on each web application requires 1
GB of memory.
The Azure subscription contains the resources in the following table.
The network security team implements several network security groups (NSGs)
Requirements
Planned Changes
Litware plans to implement the following changes:
• Deploy Azure ExpressRoute to the Montreal office.
• Migrate the virtual machines hosted on Server1 and Server2 to Azure.
• Synchronize on-premises Active Directory to Azure Active Directory (Azure AD).
• Migrate App1 and App2 to two Azure web apps named WebApp1 and WebApp2.
Technical Requirements
Litware must meet the following technical requirements:
• Ensure that WebApp1 can adjust the number of instances automatically based on the load and can scale
• up to five instances.
• Ensure that VM3 can establish outbound connections over TCP port 8080 to the applications servers in the

• Montreal office.
• Ensure that routing information is exchanged automatically between Azure and the routers in the Montreal
• office.
• Enable Azure Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) for the users in the finance department only.
• Ensure that webapp2.azurewebsites.net can be accessed by using the name app2.litware.com.
• Connect the New York office to VNet1 over the Internet by using an encrypted connection.
• Create a workflow to send an email message when the settings of VM4 are modified.
• Create a custom Azure role named Role1 that is based on the Reader role.
• Minimize costs whenever possible.

Scenario:

specific applications, or other conditions.

Litware, Inc. is a consulting company that has a main office in Montreal and two branch offices in Seattle and

200 employees.

litware.onmicrosoft.com. The tenant uses the Premium P1 pricing tier.
Existing Environment
The network contains an Active Directory forest named litware.com. All domain controllers are configured as
DNS servers and host the litware.com DNS zone.
Litware has finance, human resources, sales, research, and information technology departments. Each
department has an organizational unit (OU) that contains all the accounts of that respective department. All
the
user accounts have the department attribute set to their respective department. New users are added
frequently.
Litware.com contains a user named User1.
All the offices connect by using private connections.
Litware has data centers in the Montreal and Seattle offices. Each office has a firewall that can be configured
as a VPN device.
All infrastructure servers are virtualized. The virtualization environment contains the servers in the following

Litware uses two web applications named App1 and App2. Each instance on each web application requires 1

The network security team implements several network security groups (NSGs)

Planned Changes

Litware plans to implement the following changes:
• Deploy Azure ExpressRoute to the Montreal office.
• Migrate the virtual machines hosted on Server1 and Server2 to Azure.

Technical Requirements
Litware must meet the following technical requirements:
• Ensure that WebApp1 can adjust the number of instances automatically based on the load and can scale
• up to five instances.
• Ensure that VM3 can establish outbound connections over TCP port 8080 to the applications servers in the
• Montreal office.

• office.

Question: 609 CertyIQ
You download an Azure Resource Manager template based on an existing virtual machine. The template will be
used to deploy 100 virtual machines.
You need to modify the template to reference an administrative password. You must prevent the password from
being stored in plain text.
What should you use to store the password?
A. an Azure Key Vault and an access configuration
B. an Azure Storage account and an access policy
C. a Recovery Services vault and a backup policy
D. Microsoft Entra ID Protection and an Azure policy
Answer: A
Explanation:
A. ✅ Correct
an Azure Key Vault and an access configuration

Azure Key Vault securely stores secrets like passwords and allows ARM templates to reference them without
exposing plain text.
B. ❌ Incorrect
an Azure Storage account and an access policy
Storage accounts are not designed for secure secret management.
C. ❌ Incorrect
a Recovery Services vault and a backup policy
This is used for backup and disaster recovery, not secret storage.
D. ❌ Incorrect
Microsoft Entra ID Protection and an Azure policy
These are for identity protection and governance, not for storing secrets.
Question: 610 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription.
you plan to deploy the following file named Fielbicep.
For each of the following statements, select Yes if the statement is true. Otherwise, select No.
NOTE: Each correct selection is worth one point.

Answer:
Explanation:
Statement 1: The name of the virtual network will be the same as the location of the resource group.
❌ No. The virtual network name is hardcoded as 'VNET1', which is a string literal. The location is set
to resourceGroup().location (e.g., 'eastus', 'westus'). A string like 'VNET1' cannot equal a location string
like 'eastus'. Therefore, this statement is false.
Statement 2: Both subnet objects will be provisioned successfully.
✅ Yes. Although the statement says "both" but the template defines three subnets, all three are valid:
Subnet-1 with 10.0.0.0/24 is within 10.0.0.0/16
Subnet-2 with 10.0.1.0/24 is within 10.0.0.0/16
Subnet-3 with 10.0.2.0/24 is within 10.0.0.0/16
There are no overlapping address ranges, and all properties are correctly formatted. The deployment will
succeed for all subnets.
Statement 3: Deploying this Bicep file will error out with an error message.
❌ No. The Bicep file is syntactically correct. It uses valid resource type
(Microsoft.Network/virtualNetworks@2022-01-01), valid properties, and correct parameter referencing. There are

no missing dependencies, circular references, or invalid values. The deployment will complete successfully
without errors.
Question: 611 CertyIQ
You are configuring Azure Monitor to collect performance data from several Azure Virtual Machines. You need to
determine the expected latency for Log data to become searchable in a Log Analytics workspace after it is
generated by the resource.
What is the typical ingestion latency for Azure Monitor Logs?
A. 1 min
B. 30 sec
C. 5-10 min
D. 30 min–1 hr
E. None
Answer: C
Explanation:
C. 5–10 min ✅ Correct.
Azure Monitor Logs typically take around 5 to 10 minutes for collected log data to become searchable in a
Log Analytics workspace after the data is generated by the resource. This time includes data collection,
processing, and indexing within Azure Monitor.
A. 1 min ❌ Incorrect.
This is faster than the normal ingestion time for Azure Monitor Logs.
B. 30 sec ❌ Incorrect.
Azure Monitor Logs do not usually become searchable within seconds.
D. 30 min–1 hr ❌ Incorrect.
Such a delay is not typical and would usually indicate a problem or exceptional condition.
E. None ❌ Incorrect.
There is always some latency before logs are available for querying.
Question: 612 CertyIQ
Your company has an Azure subscription. You need to assign permissions to a new employee to manage user
accounts and reset passwords within the tenant. You are reviewing the built-in roles available in Microsoft Entra ID.
Which of the following is NOT a built-in Microsoft Entra ID (Azure AD) role?
A. Guest
B. Global Administrator
C. Developer
D. User Administrator
E. Directory Reader

Answer: C
Explanation:
C. Developer ✅ Correct.
Developer is not a standard built-in Microsoft Entra ID administrative role. While Microsoft Entra ID includes
roles such as Application Developer or Cloud Application Administrator, there is no built-in role simply named
Developer.
A. Guest ❌ Incorrect.
Guest refers to an external user type in Microsoft Entra ID, not an administrative role, but it is still a
recognized identity type within Entra ID.
B. Global Administrator ❌ Incorrect.
This is a built-in role with full administrative privileges.
D. User Administrator ❌ Incorrect.
This built-in role manages users and can reset passwords.
E. Directory Reader ❌ Incorrect.
This is a built-in role that provides read-only access to directory information.
Question: 613 CertyIQ
You are planning the deployment of a multi-tier web application in Azure. You need to ensure that all resources for
the application can be managed, monitored, and deleted as a single entity because they share the same
deployment and retirement schedule.
Which of the following should you use to group these resources?
A. Policy
B. Tagging
C. Region
D. Resource group
E. Availability Zone
Answer: D
Explanation:
D. Resource group ✅ Correct.
A resource group in Microsoft Azure is used to logically group related resources that share the same
lifecycle, such as deployment, management, monitoring, and deletion. Resources in a resource group can be
managed together as a single entity.
A. Policy ❌ Incorrect.
Azure Policy is used to enforce rules and compliance, not to group resources.
B. Tagging ❌ Incorrect.

Tags help organize and categorize resources but do not provide lifecycle management.
C. Region ❌ Incorrect.
A region defines the geographic location where resources are hosted, not how they are managed together.
E. Availability Zone ❌ Incorrect.
Availability Zones provide high availability within a region and are unrelated to grouping resources for
management.
Question: 614 CertyIQ
Your company has a hybrid cloud environment consisting of several Azure subscriptions and an on-premises data
center.
You need to implement a solution that provides a centralized platform for collecting, analyzing, and acting on
telemetry data from both your Azure resources and your on-premises servers to maximize the availability and
performance of your applications.
Which service should you use?
A. Azure Monitor
B. Azure Advisor
C. Log Analytics workspace
D. Microsoft Defender for Cloud (formerly Security Center)
E. Microsoft Sentinel
Answer: A
Explanation:
A. Azure Monitor ✅ Correct.
Azure Monitor is the centralized monitoring service in Azure that collects, analyzes, and acts on telemetry
data from both Azure resources and on-premises environments. It helps maximize the availability and
performance of applications by monitoring metrics, logs, alerts, and diagnostics across hybrid environments.
B. Azure Advisor ❌ Incorrect.
Azure Advisor provides recommendations for cost optimization, security, reliability, and performance, but it is
not the primary telemetry collection and monitoring platform.
C. Log Analytics workspace ❌ Incorrect.
A Log Analytics workspace stores and queries log data, but it is a component of Azure Monitor rather than the
complete monitoring solution.
D. Microsoft Defender for Cloud ❌ Incorrect.
Defender for Cloud focuses mainly on security posture management and threat protection.
E. Microsoft Sentinel ❌ Incorrect.
Microsoft Sentinel is a SIEM and SOAR solution used primarily for security analytics and threat detection, not
general infrastructure and application monitoring.

Question: 615 CertyIQ
You have an Azure Storage account named storage1. You plan to use storage1 to store large amounts of analytical
data. You need to ensure that storage1 can support a maximum capacity of 5 PB.
What should you do?
A. Upgrade the storage account to StorageV2 (general purpose v2).
B. Set the performance to Premium.
C. Enable hierarchical namespace.
D. Change the Replication setting.
E. Contact Microsoft Support to increase the limit.
Answer: E
Explanation:
A. Upgrade the storage account to StorageV2 (general purpose v2) ❌ Incorrect.
Upgrading to StorageV2 enables features like access tiers and lifecycle management for analytics workloads,
but it does not change the default capacity quota of 5 PiB.
B. Set the performance to Premium ❌ Incorrect.
Premium performance is designed for low-latency transactions with much lower capacity limits, making it
counterproductive for reaching 5 PB.
C. Enable hierarchical namespace ❌ Incorrect.
Enabling hierarchical namespace adds ADLS Gen2 file-system features for analytics, but it does not increase
the storage account's capacity quota.
D. Change the Replication setting ❌ Incorrect.
Replication settings (LRS, GRS, ZRS) affect data durability and disaster recovery, not the maximum storage
capacity quota.
E. Contact Microsoft Support to increase the limit ✅ Correct.
The default capacity quota varies by region (2 PB in US/Europe, 500 TB elsewhere), so reaching 5 PB requires
a formal support request for a quota increase.
Question: 616 CertyIQ
You have a Recovery Services vault that protects several Azure Virtual Machines. You modify the existing backup
policy to reduce the retention period for daily backups from 30 days to 14 days. You notice that the old recovery
points (older than 14 days) are still visible in the Azure portal.
How long does it typically take for policy changes related to the pruning of expired recovery points to take effect?
A. 1 hour
B. 30 minutes
C. 24 hours
D. Immediately
E. 5 hours

Answer: C
Explanation:
A. 1 hour ❌ Incorrect.
Backup policy changes are not processed within 1 hour; Azure Backup requires additional time to propagate
changes across the backup infrastructure.
B. 30 minutes ❌ Incorrect.
Half an hour is insufficient for backup policy modifications to fully apply, as the system needs to update
schedules and retention rules.
C. 24 hours ✅ Correct.
Changes to backup policies (such as modification of backup frequency, retention range, or vault-level
settings) typically take up to 24 hours to fully propagate and take effect across all associated backup items.
D. Immediately ❌ Incorrect.
Policy changes do not apply instantly; Azure Backup requires time to validate and apply the new configuration
to existing and future backup jobs.
E. 5 hours ❌ Incorrect.
While changes may sometimes apply sooner, the documented and reliable time frame for policy changes to
fully take effect is 24 hours, not 5 hours.
Question: 617 CertyIQ
You have a virtual machine named VM1 that uses an unmanaged remote disk stored in a storage account named
storage1.
You need to copy the VHD file of the disk to a new storage account named storage2.
The solution must ensure that the copy operation is performed directly between the storage accounts and that
access to storage1 is limited to the duration of the copy.
Which command should you run?
A. azcopy copy "[https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds/vm1.vhd]
(https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds/vm1.vhd)" "[https://storage2.blob.core.windows.net/vhds]
(https://storage2.blob.core.windows.net/vhds)"
B. az storage blob copy start-batch --source-uri "[https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds]
(https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds)" --destination-container vhds
C. azcopy copy "[https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds/vm1.vhd]
(https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds/vm1.vhd)?[SAS]" "[https://storage2.blob.core.windows.net/vhds]
(https://storage2.blob.core.windows.net/vhds)"
D. az storage blob copy start --source-uri "[https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds]
(https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds)" --destination-container vhds
Answer: C
Explanation:
A. azcopy copy "https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds/vm1.vhd"
"https://storage2.blob.core.windows.net/vhds" ❌ Incorrect.
This command lacks a SAS token on the source URL, which means full authentication would be required, and

it does not limit access to storage1 to only the duration of the copy operation.
B. az storage blob copy start-batch --source-uri "https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds" --
destination-container vhds ❌ Incorrect.
This command uses start-batch which is for multiple blobs and does not specify a SAS token; also, the source
URI points to the container, not the specific VHD file.
C. azcopy copy "https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds/vm1.vhd?[SAS]"
"https://storage2.blob.core.windows.net/vhds" ✅ Correct.
The SAS token appended to the source URL provides time-limited, permission-restricted access to only the
specific VHD blob, and AzCopy performs a direct server-side copy between storage accounts without
downloading the file locally.
D. az storage blob copy start --source-uri "https://storage1.blob.core.windows.net/vhds" --destination-
container vhds ❌ Incorrect.
This command is missing the SAS token for limited access and the source URI points to the container instead
of the individual VHD file; also, it lacks the destination blob name.
Question: 618 CertyIQ
You have an Azure Storage account named storage1 that contains several containers. You need to implement a
solution to reduce storage costs. The solution must ensure that any blobs in storage1 that have not been modified
for more than 30 days are automatically moved from the Hot tier to the Archive tier.
What should you configure for storage1?
A. A private endpoint
B. Public network access in the Firewalls and virtual networks setting
C. A shared access signature (SAS)
D. A Lifecycle management rule
Answer: D
Explanation:
A. A private endpoint ❌ Incorrect.
A private endpoint enables secure access to storage1 over a private IP address within your virtual network, but
it does not manage data movement between access tiers or time-based transitions.
B. Public network access in the Firewalls and virtual networks setting ❌ Incorrect.
Public network access controls which networks can connect to storage1, affecting security and accessibility
only, with no ability to automate tier transitions based on age.
C. A shared access signature (SAS) ❌ Incorrect.
A SAS token provides delegated, time-limited permission to specific storage resources, but it does not
configure automatic data movement to Archive tier after any duration.
D. Lifecycle management ✅ Correct.
Lifecycle management is an Azure Blob Storage feature that automates data tier transitions (e.g., Hot → Cool
→ Archive) or deletion based on age rules, such as moving blobs to Archive tier after 30 days of creation or

last modification.
Question: 619 CertyIQ
You have an Azure storage account that contains a large amount of data.
You need to ensure that you can access the data from an on-premises computer by using a drive letter.
What should you include in the solution?
A. A Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN connection
B. An Azure File sync agent
C. A shared access policy
D. A Microsoft Azure Storage Explorer
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is actually A. A Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN connection.
Here is why A is the intended answer for the exam, and why the logic shifts when looking at Microsoft's
official constraints:
The Core Problem: Port 445 (SMB)
To map a traditional drive letter (like Z:) directly to an Azure File Share from an on-premises computer,
Windows uses the SMB protocol.
SMB natively communicates over Port 445. However, almost all residential and commercial Internet Service
Providers (ISPs) strictly block Port 445 outbound to the public internet for security reasons (to prevent
malware like WannaCry).
Why A (Site-to-Site VPN) is the Key
By establishing a Site-to-Site (S2S) VPN connection (or an ExpressRoute), you create a secure, private tunnel
between your on-premises network and the Azure Virtual Network.
Because the traffic travels inside an encrypted VPN tunnel, it bypasses the ISP's public internet port blocking.
The on-premises computer can now communicate directly with the Azure Storage account's private endpoint
or service endpoint over Port 445.
This securely allows the user to run the net use Z: \\storageaccount.file.core.windows.net\share command and
successfully map the drive letter.
Why B (Azure File Sync Agent) is a Distractor Here
While Azure File Sync is a great real-world solution for caching Azure Files on-premises, it fails the question's
criteria for two reasons:
The Question Specifies "an on-premises computer": The Azure File Sync Agent can only be installed on
Windows Server operating systems. You cannot install it on standard client machines (Windows 10/11) to
natively map a drive.
Architecture Flow: With File Sync, users map their drive letter to the local Windows Server share, not to the
Azure Storage account directly.

Question: 620 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains a storage account named account1.
You plan to upload the disk files of an on-premises virtual machine to account1. The on-premises network uses a
public IP address of 131.107.1.5. You will use the Azure Import/Export service and the WAImportExport.exe tool on
an on-premises server named Server1.
You need to configure account1 to meet the following requirements:
Ensure that you can upload the disk files to account1.
Ensure that you can attach the disk files to an Azure VM after the import.
Prevent all other access to the account from the internet.
Which two actions should you perform? Each correct selection forms part of the solution.
A. From the Networking blade of account1, select Selected networks and add the 131.107.1.5 IP address.
B. From the Networking blade of account1, select Enabled from selected virtual networks and IP addresses.
C. From the Networking blade of account1, select Allow Azure services on the trusted services list to access
this storage account.
D. From the Networking blade of account1, add the 10.10.0.0/16 address range.
E. From the Configuration blade of account1, set Allow trusted Microsoft services to Enabled.
Answer: A,E
Explanation:
To lock down the storage account (account1) according to the principles of least privilege while ensuring that
the data import and VM creation tasks succeed, you must isolate the firewall configurations carefully:
Allowing the On-Premises Upload (Option A): The WAImportExport.exe tool requires network access from
your on-premises server (Server1) to build and submit the data-plane parameters and journal files directly to
the storage account. To isolate this traffic while restricting all other public internet access, you change the
firewall default action to Selected networks and explicitly whitelist the on-premises environment's public
outbound IP address (131.107.1.5).
Allowing Azure VM Disk Attachment (Option E): Once the physical disks are shipped, processed, and
available in your storage account as blobs, the Azure platform itself needs underlying management fabric
permissions to attach those blobs to a compute instance as virtual machine disks. By enabling Allow trusted
Microsoft services (under the Configuration or Networking exceptions panel depending on the portal
interface version), you grant the inner Azure deployment orchestrator permission to securely bypass the
firewall rule and bind the disk files to your destination virtual machine.
### Why the Other Options Are Incorrect
B. Select "Enabled from selected virtual networks and IP addresses": While conceptually describing the
selection process, the definitive option statement in the interface framework requires clicking the Selected
networks toggle button under the network routing matrix.
C. Allow Azure services on the trusted services list...: While this is a step taken under the "Exceptions"
header, the exact terminology mapped across the foundational control settings panel explicitly uses the
billing and management resource parameter Allow trusted Microsoft services.
D. Add the 10.10.0.0/16 address range: This specifies a private IP space (RFC 1918). Azure Storage account
firewalls do not accept on-premises private internal subnets directly; they require either public IP endpoints
or routed Azure Virtual Network subnets (VNets) via Service Endpoints.

Question: 621 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains an Azure SQL database named SQL1.
You plan to create an Azure automation account named Automation1.
Automation1 will contain a runbook that will backup SQL1 to an Azure storage account.
You need to configure a storage account for Automation1.
What should you use?
A. Azure Table storage
B. Azure Blob storage
C. Azure Queue storage
D. Azure Files
Answer: B
Explanation:
A. Azure Table storage Incorrect.
Table storage is a NoSQL key-value store designed for semi-structured data, not for storing database backup
files which are large, unstructured binary objects.
B. Azure Blob storage Correct.
Azure Blob storage is designed for storing large amounts of unstructured data, including database backup
files (.bacpac, .bak files), and is the standard destination for Azure SQL database backups from Automation
runbooks.
C. Azure Queue storage Incorrect.
Queue storage is used for message queuing between application components for asynchronous processing,
not for storing backup files.
D. Azure Files Incorrect.
Azure Files provides fully managed SMB file shares for lift-and-shift applications, but it is not the typical or
recommended destination for automated SQL database backups from Azure Automation runbooks.
Question: 622 CertyIQ
You have an existing Azure virtual machine named VM1 that is currently running. You need to perform several
administrative tasks on the VM.
Which of the following changes will require VM1 to be restarted, resulting in temporary downtime?
A. Add a 500 GB managed disk to the VM.
B. Change the size of the VM to DS2_v2.
C. Add the Puppet Agent extension to the VM.
D. Change the "License type" for Windows Server to use Azure Hybrid Benefit.
Answer: B
Explanation:
A. Add a 500 GB managed disk to the VM Incorrect.

Adding a new managed disk to a running Azure VM is a hot-add operation that occurs without restarting the
VM; the disk becomes available immediately after attachment.
B. Change the size of the VM to DS2_v2 Correct.
Changing a VM's size requires the VM to be in a stopped (deallocated) state before the resize operation, which
means the VM must be shut down, resulting in temporary downtime.
C. Add the Puppet Agent extension to the VM Incorrect.
VM extensions, including the Puppet Agent, are installed on running VMs without requiring a restart; the
extension agent handles the installation dynamically.
D. Change the "License type" for Windows Server to use Azure Hybrid Benefit Incorrect.
Modifying the license type (Azure Hybrid Benefit) is a simple metadata change that takes effect immediately
without restarting the VM; it only affects billing and licensing compliance.
Question: 623 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains a resource group named RG1. RG1 contains an Azure virtual machine
named VM1.
You plan to implement a backup solution for VM1. You create a new Recovery Services vault named Vault1 in RG1.
You need to ensure that you can configure the backup of VM1 to Vault1.
What should you do first?
A. Add the Azure Backup Discovery service tag to RG1.
B. Add VM1 to a Virtual Machine Scale Set.
C. Install the Microsoft Azure Recovery Services (MARS) agent on VM1.
D. Modify the IAM role-based access control (RBAC) assignments for Vault1.
E. Register the Microsoft.RecoveryServices resource provider.
Answer: E
Explanation:
A. Add the Azure Backup Discovery service tag to RG1 Incorrect.
Service tags control network traffic, not backup configuration; they are unrelated to enabling or configuring
Recovery Services vault backups.
B. Add VM1 to a Virtual Machine Scale Set Incorrect.
Adding VM1 to a scale set would change its deployment model and is not required for backup; Azure Backup
works with individual VMs regardless of scale set membership.
C. Install the Microsoft Azure Recovery Services (MARS) agent on VM1 Incorrect.
The MARS agent is used for backing up files, folders, and system state, not for Azure VM backups; Azure VM
backup uses the VM snapshot extension (managed by Azure Backup fabric), not manual agent installation.
D. Modify the IAM role-based access control (RBAC) assignments for Vault1 Incorrect.
IAM permissions control who can manage backup operations, but this is not a prerequisite for configuring
backup; the resource provider registration must happen first.

E. Register the Microsoft.RecoveryServices resource provider Correct.
Before using any Recovery Services vault features, the Microsoft.RecoveryServices resource provider must be
registered in your subscription; this is typically done automatically when creating Vault1, but if not, it must be
registered first to enable backup configuration.
Question: 624 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription. You plan to deploy an Azure Firewall to a virtual network named VNET1. You need
to ensure that the environment is prepared for the deployment.
What is a requirement for deploying an Azure Firewall in VNET1?
A. An Azure Firewall policy is required for each Azure region.
B. An Azure Firewall must join an existing subnet that contains other virtual machines in VNET1.
C. An Azure Firewall must be associated with a Network Security Group (NSG) before deployment.
D. An Azure Firewall requires a dedicated subnet named AzureFirewallSubnet.
Answer: D
Explanation:
A. An Azure Firewall policy is required for each Azure region Incorrect.
A firewall policy is associated with the firewall but can be shared across multiple firewalls in different
regions; it is not a deployment prerequisite for the Azure Firewall resource itself.
B. An Azure Firewall must join an existing subnet that contains other virtual machines in VNET1 Incorrect.
Azure Firewall requires its own dedicated subnet and cannot share a subnet with other resources like virtual
machines or gateways.
C. An Azure Firewall must be associated with a Network Security Group (NSG) before deployment
Incorrect.
Azure Firewall is itself a network security service; it does not require an NSG, and in fact, associating an NSG
with the AzureFirewallSubnet is unsupported and may break the firewall.
D. An Azure Firewall requires a dedicated subnet named AzureFirewallSubnet Correct.
Azure Firewall must be deployed into a subnet named exactly AzureFirewallSubnet (or
AzureFirewallManagementSubnet for forced tunneling mode), and this subnet cannot contain any other
resources.
Question: 625 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription and a local Docker image named image1:v1. You create an Azure Container Registry
named Registry1 that has a login server address of registry1.azurecr.io.
You need to push image1:v1 to Registry1.
Which action should you perform first?
A. Tag the local image as registry1.azurecr.io/image1:v1.
B. Enable the Admin user account for Registry1.
C. Create an Azure Container Instance (ACI) group.

D. Run the docker push registry1 command.
Answer: A
Explanation:
A. Tag the local image as registry1.azurecr.io/image1:v1 Correct.
Before pushing, you must tag your local image with the ACR login server address (registry1.azurecr.io) so that
Docker knows which registry to push to; the command is docker tag image1:v1 registry1.azurecr.io/image1:v1.
B. Enable the Admin user account for Registry1 Incorrect.
While enabling the admin account provides username/password authentication, this is not the first action;
tagging the image comes first, and authentication (via docker login) happens immediately before pushing.
C. Create an Azure Container Instance (ACI) group Incorrect.
Creating an ACI group is unrelated to pushing images to ACR; ACI is for running containers, not storing or
pushing images.
D. Run the docker push registry1 command Incorrect.
The docker push command requires a full image name including tag (e.g., registry1.azurecr.io/image1:v1); you
cannot push just by specifying the registry name, and tagging must occur first.
Question: 626 CertyIQ
You have an Azure tenant that contains a resource group named RG1.
You plan to implement an Azure Troubleshooter for RG1. You need to ensure that the troubleshooter can identify
all common configuration issues for RG1.
What should you include in the troubleshooter?
A. Only enable insights
B. Two-variable analysis
C. One-facet analysis
D. Inter-facet discovery
Answer: D
Explanation:
A. Only enable insights Incorrect.
Enabling insights alone provides monitoring data and recommendations, but it does not perform
comprehensive configuration issue detection across multiple resource types in a resource group.
B. Two-variable analysis Incorrect.
Two-variable analysis is a statistical technique, not an Azure Troubleshooter capability for identifying
configuration issues across diverse resources in RG1.
C. One-facet analysis Incorrect.
One-facet analysis limits troubleshooting to a single aspect or dimension of a resource, which is insufficient

for identifying all common configuration issues across multiple resource types in RG1.
D. Inter-facet discovery Correct.
Inter-facet discovery analyzes relationships and interactions between different facets (aspects) of resources
within RG1, enabling the troubleshooter to identify configuration issues that span multiple resources, such as
networking misconfigurations, RBAC inconsistencies, and dependency problems.
Question: 627 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains a user named User1.
User1 is assigned the Reader role for the subscription.
You need to ensure that the developer of User1 can create new Azure logic apps in the subscription and must
follow the principle of least privilege.
What should you do?
A. Assign the Website Contributor role to the developer.
B. Configure a just-in-time (JIT) role for User1.
C. Assign the Logic App Contributor role to the developer.
D. Configure a just-in-time (JIT) role for the developer.
Answer: C
Explanation:
A. Assign the Website Contributor role to the developer Incorrect.
The Website Contributor role manages web apps (App Service), not logic apps; it does not grant permissions
to create or manage Azure Logic Apps.
B. Configure a just-in-time (JIT) role for User1 Incorrect.
JIT access is for temporarily elevating permissions (typically for VMs or management plane access), not for
granting ongoing permissions to create logic apps; also, User1 already has Reader access, but the developer
needs Logic App permissions.
C. Assign the Logic App Contributor role to the developer Correct.
The Logic App Contributor role grants exactly the permissions needed to create, read, update, and delete
logic apps, following the principle of least privilege by providing only logic app management capabilities.
D. Configure a just-in-time (JIT) role for the developer Incorrect.
While JIT can provide temporary access, the requirement is for the developer to create logic apps (presumably
ongoing work), not time-limited access; JIT also does not directly grant Logic App permissions.
Question: 628 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains an Azure storage account named storage1. A development team is
deploying an application that writes logs to storage1. The storage account is currently configured as follows:
Performance: Standard
Replication: Geo-redundant storage (GRS)
You need to ensure that the application can continue to read the logs even if the primary Azure region becomes
unavailable. The solution must minimize administrative effort.Which two actions should you perform?

Each correct answer presents part of the solution.
A. Display the Access keys to incorporate into connection strings.
B. Initiate a manual failover of the storage account.
C. Keep the replication as GRS.
D. Update the replication to Read-access geo-redundant storage (RA-GRS).
E. Update the application to use the secondary endpoint for read operations.
Answer: D,E
Explanation:
A. Display the Access keys to incorporate into connection strings Incorrect.
Access keys are used for authentication, not for enabling read access during a regional outage; they do not
affect failover or read capabilities from the secondary region.
B. Initiate a manual failover of the storage account Incorrect.
Manual failover promotes the secondary region to primary, but it requires active intervention during an outage
and causes downtime during the failover process; this does not minimize administrative effort.
C. Keep the replication as GRS Incorrect.
GRS replicates data to a secondary region, but the secondary replica is not directly readable unless a failover
occurs; applications cannot read logs from the secondary region during an outage with GRS alone.
D. Update the replication to Read-access geo-redundant storage (RA-GRS) Correct.
RA-GRS provides all the benefits of GRS (geo-replication) plus read access to the secondary region, allowing
applications to read data from the secondary endpoint even when the primary region is unavailable.
E. Update the application to use the secondary endpoint for read operations Correct.
With RA-GRS enabled, the application must be configured to use the secondary endpoint (storage1-
secondary.blob.core.windows.net) for read operations during a primary region outage; this enables continuous
log reading without manual failover.
Question: 629 CertyIQ
You have a Microsoft 365 tenant and an Azure subscription. You enable Microsoft Entra ID Protection.
You need to ensure that when a user is flagged for "User risk," they are automatically prompted to perform a self-
service password reset (SSPR) to remediate the risk.
The solution must minimize administrative effort.What should you do in the Microsoft Entra admin center?
A. From the User risk policy settings, configure the Access control setting.
B. From the Sign-in risk policy settings, configure the Access control setting.
C. From the User risk policy settings, configure the Conditions setting.
D. From the Sign-in risk policy settings, configure the Conditions setting.
Answer: A
Explanation:

A. From the User risk policy settings, configure the Access control setting Correct.
The User risk policy applies to user accounts that are flagged as risky. Within the policy's Access control
setting, you can configure "Allow access" with the requirement to "Require password change" (self-service
password reset), which automatically prompts users to remediate their risk.
B. From the Sign-in risk policy settings, configure the Access control setting Incorrect.
Sign-in risk policy applies to suspicious authentication attempts (e.g., anonymous IP, atypical travel), not to
user account risk levels; it cannot trigger SSPR for user risk remediation.
C. From the User risk policy settings, configure the Conditions setting Incorrect.
The Conditions setting defines which users or risk levels the policy applies to (e.g., "Risk level: Medium and
above"), not the remediation action; Access control determines what happens when the condition is met.
D. From the Sign-in risk policy settings, configure the Conditions setting Incorrect.
This configures conditions for sign-in risk, not user risk, and Conditions alone does not set the SSPR
remediation action.
Question: 630 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains an Azure container registry named Registry1.The subscription
contains an Azure virtual machine named VM1 that runs Windows Server 2019.VM1 is configured to use a managed
identity.You need to ensure that you can pull images from Registry1 to VM1.
What should you do?
A. Assign the AcrPull role and specify the system-assigned managed identity as the principal.
B. Assign the Reader role and specify the user-assigned managed identity as the principal.
C. Create a key, upload the key to VM1, and use the Azure container registry login server.
D. Create a user, assign the user to the VM1, and use the Azure container registry login server.
Answer: A
Explanation:
A. Assign the AcrPull role and specify the system-assigned managed identity as the principal Correct.
The AcrPull role grants exactly the permission needed to pull images from a container registry. Assigning this
role to VM1's system-assigned managed identity allows VM1 to authenticate with Registry1 using its managed
identity without storing any credentials.
B. Assign the Reader role and specify the user-assigned managed identity as the principal Incorrect.
The Reader role does not grant permissions to pull images from a container registry; it only allows viewing
registry metadata. Additionally, VM1 is configured with a system-assigned managed identity, not a user-
assigned identity.
C. Create a key, upload the key to VM1, and use the Azure container registry login server Incorrect.
Using access keys requires storing and managing secrets on VM1, which increases administrative overhead
and security risk; managed identities eliminate the need for key management and are the recommended
approach.
D. Create a user, assign the user to VM1, and use the Azure container registry login server Incorrect.

Creating a user account and assigning it to VM1 is not a standard pattern for Azure VM access to ACR;
managed identities provide secure, credential-free authentication without creating or managing user
accounts.
Question: 631 CertyIQ
You have a virtual machine named VM1. You create a new Azure Backup policy.You need to configure the policy to
automatically back up VM1.
To what should you add VM1?
A. backup policy backup guide
B. Resource tag
C. Recovery Services vault
D. Pool
Answer: C
Explanation:
A. Backup policy backup guide Incorrect.
A backup policy defines the schedule and retention settings (e.g., daily backup at 10 PM, keep for 30 days),
but it is not the location where you add VMs; you associate VMs with a policy through the Recovery Services
vault.
B. Resource tag Incorrect.
Resource tags are metadata labels for organizing Azure resources (e.g., "Environment=Production"), not a
mechanism for attaching VMs to backup policies or enabling automated backups.
C. Recovery Services vault Correct.
The Recovery Services vault is the management container where you add VM1, associate it with the backup
policy, and configure automated backups; you navigate to the vault, select "Backup," choose the VM, and
apply the policy.
D. Pool Incorrect.
Pools are used in Azure Batch, Azure VM Scale Sets, or other services for resource allocation, not for backup
configuration; Backup does not use any "pool" concept.
Question: 632 CertyIQ
This question is part of a series of questions that present the same scenario.
Each question in the series contains a unique solution that might meet the stated goals.
Some question sets might have more than one correct solution, while others might not have a correct
solution.After you answer a question in this section, you will NOT be able to return to it.
As a result, these questions will not appear in the review screen.Scenario:You have an Azure storage account
named storage1.
You created a lifecycle management rule for storage1 that moves blobs to cool storage after 30 days.You receive a
notification that storage1 will be affected by maintenance.
You need to move storage1 to a different Azure availability zone.Solution: From the storage account, you modify
the replication setting.
Does this meet the goal?

A. Yes
B. No
Answer: B
Explanation:
A. Yes Incorrect.
Modifying the replication setting alone does not move an existing storage account to a different availability
zone; replication settings control how data is copied for durability (LRS, ZRS, GRS, etc.), not the physical
location of the primary storage account.
B. No Correct.
Changing the replication setting (e.g., from LRS to ZRS) may enable zone-redundant storage, but it does not
move the existing storage account's primary region or availability zone. To move a storage account to a
different availability zone, you would need to create a new storage account in the target zone and migrate the
data manually or use tools like AzCopy.
Question: 633 CertyIQ
Your company has an on-premises Active Directory Domain Services (AD DS) domain that contains 500 user
accounts, 20 security groups, and 300 Windows 11 computers. You plan to implement Microsoft Entra Connect to
synchronize the on-premises objects to Microsoft Entra ID.
By default, which object types will be synchronized to Microsoft Entra ID?
A. User accounts and groups only.
B. User accounts and devices only.
C. User accounts, groups, and devices only.
D. User accounts, groups, and contacts only.
E. User accounts, groups, and the devices that are joined to a domain.
Answer: D
Explanation:
A. User accounts and groups only Incorrect.
While user accounts and groups are synchronized by default, this option omits contacts, which are also
synchronized by default from the on-premises AD DS environment.
B. User accounts and devices only Incorrect.
Devices (computers) are not synchronized by default; they require additional configuration such as Hybrid
Azure AD Join. Also, groups and contacts are missing from this option.
C. User accounts, groups, and devices only Incorrect.
Devices are not synchronized by default, and contacts (which are synchronized by default) are incorrectly
omitted.
D. User accounts, groups, and contacts only Correct.

By default, Microsoft Entra Connect synchronizes user accounts, security groups, distribution groups, and
contacts. Devices (including Windows 11 computers) are not synchronized unless you enable Hybrid Azure AD
Join or device writeback.
E. User accounts, groups, and the devices that are joined to a domain Incorrect.
Domain-joined devices are not synchronized by default; this requires explicit configuration of Hybrid Azure AD
Join.
Question: 634 CertyIQ
You have an Azure subscription that contains several virtual networks and storage accounts. You need to ensure
that all resource logs and metrics for the storage accounts are sent to a Log Analytics workspace for custom
querying and long-term retention.
What should you include in the recommendation?
A. Azure Log Analytics
B. Azure Application Insights
C. Azure Active Directory (Azure AD) Reporting
D. Azure Monitor metric alerts
E. Azure Monitor diagnostic settings
Answer: E
Explanation:
A. Azure Log Analytics Incorrect.
Log Analytics is the workspace where data is stored and queried, but it is not the configuration tool that sends
data from storage accounts to the workspace; diagnostic settings are used to configure the data transfer.
B. Azure Application Insights Incorrect.
Application Insights is designed for monitoring application performance and usage (application-level
telemetry), not for collecting resource logs and metrics from Azure storage accounts.
C. Azure Active Directory (Azure AD) Reporting Incorrect.
Azure AD Reporting provides sign-in logs and audit logs for identity and access management, not for storage
account resource logs or metrics.
D. Azure Monitor metric alerts Incorrect.
Metric alerts notify you when specific metrics cross a threshold (e.g., CPU > 80%), but they do not send logs or
metrics to a Log Analytics workspace for storage and querying.
E. Azure Monitor diagnostic settings Correct.
Diagnostic settings in Azure Monitor allow you to configure which platform logs and metrics from storage
accounts (and other Azure resources) are sent to destination(s) including a Log Analytics workspace for
custom querying and long-term retention.
